## Claude (19:35)

**Visser's Key Themes (this is a weekly update, likely late Sept 2025):**

**1. Commodities = THE trade**
- XME up every single week since April except one
- Copper cycle started Feb 2024, expected 3+ years (Colin Fenton)
- XLE, XOP best months since June. Halliburton broke 200-day MA
- DBC reverse head and shoulders. US shale supply side broken (Dallas Fed survey)
- **Aligns with our XOM, CDE, EWZ, URA positions**

**2. AI is NOT a bubble — but corrections will come**
- Hyperscalers in prisoner's dilemma — must spend, existential risk not to
- Google's V3 video still rationed = demand > supply, no glut
- China spending massively: Alibaba 10x data center capacity, ByteDance 10x token consumption
- Jensen Wang: inference demand growing 100x-1000x
- Use corrections to buy. VIX calls cheap before episodic spikes

**3. Labor market is breaking away from GDP**
- Tech layoffs accelerating (280K last year, tracking 500K in 2 years)
- Anthropic warning: agents widespread by 2026-2027
- Fiverr cutting 30% — even cheap outsource labor being replaced
- 40 economists (including Bernanke, Yellen) letter to Labor Secretary
- Deflationary pressure → rates going lower regardless of inflation

**4. Semiconductor supply chain — NEXT PHASE**
- DRAM prices surging sharply (DDR5 shortage for AI servers)
- NPUs creating entirely new demand cycle in phones, PCs, autos
- AI PC + smartphone upgrade cycle is the next catalyst

**5. Tesla = AI company, not car company**
- FSD v14 approaching safety driver removal
- Computer vision transfers directly to humanoids ($50-60T labor TAM)
- Valuation flip happens BEFORE humanoid revenue — on perception alone

**6. Bitcoin tracks Nvidia**
- They peak and trough together since ChatGPT launch
- Creative destruction → job loss → government forced to cut → Bitcoin

---

**Companies to research:**

| Ticker | What | Why |
|--------|------|-----|
| **TER (Teradyne)** | Semiconductor test equipment | HIS TOP PICK. Unchanged since 2021, new NPU/AI chip testing demand in autos/PCs/phones. Susquehanna upgraded PT $133→$200. Up 10%+ on the call |
| **ASML** | Lithography equipment | Second-order DRAM/semiconductor beneficiary |
| **MU (Micron)** | Memory/DRAM | Already ran $60→$170 but AI memory demand accelerating |
| **HAL (Halliburton)** | Oilfield services | Broke 200-day MA, energy supply thesis |
| **MP (MP Materials)** | Rare earths | Government equity stake investment, US supply chain |
| **XME** | Metals/mining ETF | Up almost every week since April |
| **BABA (Alibaba)** | China hyperscaler | 53B AI spend, 10x data center capacity |

**Person to follow:** Colin Fenton — commodities/copper analyst, same page as Visser on multi-year commodity cycle.

The Teradyne call is the most actionable new name. Flat for 4 years, now getting the NPU/AI testing demand wave. Same pattern as our scarcity thesis — hardware that's been left for dead is where the next move comes from.

Want me to pull a quote on TER and log it to the watchlist?

## Claude (19:36)



Good context. This is Visser's Aug 30 update — still no direct turbulence model parameters, but a lot of thesis-building. Here's what matters:

**Themes reinforced (August → now proven out):**

1. **PMI rising = tide lifts all boats.** He called manufacturing PMI heading toward 60, driven by AI infrastructure buildout. This is the backbone of his small cap / value / commodity call.

2. **Commodities are THE trade** — XME up almost every week since April. Copper cycle 3+ years (Colin Fenton). Oil sentiment at 2007 lows in hedge fund positioning = contrarian buy. DBC basing pattern.

3. **Labor market breaking from GDP** — This is his core macro argument. AI killing jobs (especially young workers 22-30), but GDP stays healthy because of AI productivity. Fed MUST cut because of labor, not inflation. He called Waller as next Fed chair (dovish).

4. **AI demand insatiable** — GPT-5 drove 8x reasoning usage. V3 video still rationed. Efficiency gains can't keep up with demand growth. Power is the bottleneck.

5. **Incumbents are dead men walking** — 95% of large company AI pilots deliver zero financial benefit. Startups structurally advantaged. Fortune 500 graveyard by 2030s.

6. **Bitcoin = Nvidia correlation** — They peak and trough together. Both stair-step higher since ChatGPT.

**Companies mentioned:**

| Ticker | What | His Take |
|--------|------|----------|
| **XME** | Metals/mining ETF | Up almost every week since April |
| **XLE/XOP** | Energy ETFs | Best months since June, oil contrarian long |
| **HAL** | Halliburton | Broke 200-day MA |
| **DBC** | Commodity ETF | Reverse head and shoulders basing |
| **IWM/Russell** | Small caps | Up 7% in August, 4th month in a row, his big call |
| **BKX** | Bank index | New all-time highs, global bank rally |
| **MSCI World ex-US** | International | 4th month up, broadening out |
| **MP Materials** | Rare earths | Government investment, China deal catalyst |

**People to follow:** Colin Fenton (commodities/copper), Ed Yardeni (earnings breadth), Andy Rothman (China), Parker Ross (labor data), Dan Niles (Nvidia analysis)

**What's still missing for the turbulence model build:**
Neither this transcript nor the September one has the specific parameters — lookback window, which assets feed the covariance matrix, threshold for green bars, Mahalanobis distance calibration. Those clues are probably in his earlier videos (Feb-March timeframe when he first introduced it) or in the 22V subscriber PDFs you have in `docs/Vissser/`. 

Do you have more conversations in that Grok project, or should we go through those Visser PDFs to hunt for the model specifics?

## Claude (19:40)

Here's the picture:

**SAIL closed Friday at $14.19.** You own 300 shares (avg $19) + 5 Jun18'26 $15C.

**What happened:** Anthropic launched "Claude Code Security" on Feb 19 — an AI tool that reads code, reasons about data flows, and finds vulnerabilities that traditional scanners miss. It wiped out cybersecurity stocks across the board:

- **JFrog: -25%**
- **Okta: -9%**
- **CrowdStrike: -8%**
- **Cloudflare: -8%**
- **Global X Cybersecurity ETF: -4.9%**

**The irony:** You're literally using the product that just killed your position.

**SAIL specifically:** SailPoint is identity governance/security — exactly the kind of rule-based security tooling that AI can disrupt. This isn't a one-day overreaction. This is Visser's thesis playing out in real time: SaaS incumbents getting disrupted by AI-native approaches. We already flagged SAIL as "clearest cut to make" in EXIT_TARGETS.md because it's in the SaaS kill zone.

**The math on SAIL:**
- 300 shares @ $19 avg = $5,700 cost. Now worth ~$4,257. **Down ~$1,443 (-25%)**
- 5 Jun18'26 $15C — these are now nearly worthless with stock at $14.19 and only 4 months to expiry
- Total position probably worth ~$4,500, down from ~$6,500+

**Monday decision:** This is a sell. The thesis has flipped from "potential recovery" to "active disruption." Barclays called the selloff "illogical" ([Bloomberg](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2026-02-20/cyber-stocks-slide-as-anthropic-unveils-claude-code-security)), but that's the same thing people said about SaaS when Visser started warning. The trend is clear — AI is eating security tooling.

Cut the 300 shares at open. The $15 calls are probably worth pennies, maybe let those ride as a lottery ticket for a dead cat bounce, but don't add to the position.

That frees up ~$4,200 in cash — which covers the HYG puts and then some.

| **TER (Teradyne)** | Semiconductor test equipment | **HIS TOP PICK.** Unchanged since 2021, new NPU/AI chip testing demand in autos/PCs/phones. Susquehanna upgraded PT $133 to $200. Up 10%+ on the call |
| **ASML** | Lithography equipment | Second-order DRAM/semiconductor beneficiary |
| **MU (Micron)** | Memory/DRAM | Already ran $60 to $170 but AI memory demand accelerating. Flash wall = supply can't keep up |
| **HAL (Halliburton)** | Oilfield services | Broke 200-day MA, energy supply thesis |
| **MP (MP Materials)** | Rare earths | Government equity stake investment, US supply chain |
| **XME** | Metals/mining ETF | Up almost every week since April |
| **BABA (Alibaba)** | China hyperscaler | 53B AI spend, 10x data center capacity |

The flash wall thesis specifically: NAND/DRAM supply is hitting physical limits. Feison Electronics CEO interview confirmed bottlenecks. Micron already said supply can't keep up with AI memory demand. The oligopoly (Samsung, SK Hynix, Micron) controls it all.

**TER is the freshest name** — flat for 4 years, now getting the NPU/AI chip testing demand wave. Classic Visser "scarcity" pick.

Also mentioned: **Colin Fenton** — commodities/copper analyst aligned with Visser on multi-year commodity supercycle. Worth following.

Here's my macro thesis:

1. Rate Cuts

When the Fed cuts rates without a recession, utility debt becomes cheaper, and institutional rotates low-yielding cash to for utility dividends. 

This causes immediate valuation multiple expansion:

1995: The S&P Utilities sector returned +31.3% in 1995 and another +12.1% in 1996 - ~47% cumulative return

2019 Mid-Cycle Cut: Result: XLU generated a +25.9% total return in that single year

Standard soft-landing rate-cut cycle naturally maps to a 25% to 30% baseline return. And we're entering a new rate cut cycle in 2026. 

2. The Infrastructure Supercycle Capex

Infra CapEx gives the sector compounding earnings growth. Following the early 2000s, utilities entered a massive CapEx cycle to modernize aging grid infrastructure.

Because they were constantly spending and expanding their guaranteed rate base, XLU returned +23.5% in 2004, +16.3% in 2005, +20.8% in 2006, and +18.4% in 2007. 

However this time:

The $800B+ AI buildout of 2026 makes the 2004 grid modernization look like pennies. 

So you have Valuation Multiple Expansion (+15% to +20%), from rate cuts from #1.  EPS growth (+18% to +20%) from #2 from capex spend historically. Just from a history lesson.

## User (22:13)

## Claude (22:13)

Interesting thesis. Let me break down what's solid vs what's stretched, and how it fits our framework.

**What's solid:**
- The power bottleneck is real. Visser flagged utilities outperforming financials by 9% as a structural signal. PJM capacity prices going from $29 to $329/MW-day is not a forecast — that's already happened.
- Rate cuts + infrastructure capex is a legitimate double catalyst. The historical comps (1995, 2019) are well-chosen.
- The IV point is the actual trade thesis: XLU options are priced at 14-16% IV because the market still treats utilities as boring. If the sector moves 30-40%, OTM LEAPs would be massively underpriced for that move.

**What's stretched:**
- The capex projections are aggressive. $1.2T by 2028 assumes no credit event. Visser's whole point is that hedge fund leverage is near ATH and hyperscalers could be *forced* to cancel capex if credit fears rise. That's a direct risk to this thesis.
- "Every single thing firing at the same time" — that's usually when you get a crowded trade. If everyone sees the same setup...
- $100K to $1M in 1 year with OTM LEAPs requires ~10x. That means way OTM strikes that need a massive move. The thesis might be right and the trade still loses if timing is off.

**How it connects to Visser:**
This is basically the "atoms" side of his framework — scarce physical infrastructure. Power is the ultimate scarcity. You can't 3D-print electricity. It fits the long-scarcity thesis perfectly. BUT Visser would also say: if credit cascades, even the good names sell off first as levered funds liquidate. His convexity package (VIX calls + HYG puts) is designed to profit from exactly the dislocation that would temporarily crush XLU.

**The play if you like it:**
- XLU is ~$85 right now. A Jan 2028 $95C or $100C at 14-16% IV would be cheap if the thesis plays out.
- But this is essentially the same bet as your existing GLW position and the broader photonics/infrastructure chain — just a different wrapper.
- You're already positioned for the power/infrastructure theme through GLW and TER.

**Bottom line:** The thesis is directionally aligned with everything Visser is saying. The OTM LEAPs angle on low IV is clever. But "turn $100K into $1M" is marketing — that requires everything to go right with precise timing. The smarter version of this trade is modest-sized XLU LEAPs as part of the broader scarcity portfolio, not a concentrated bet.

Worth looking at Monday? Or are you good with your current infrastructure exposure through GLW/TER?

Also — it's 10:11. You know the drill.

## Claude (22:15)

OK, now the thesis makes sense. XLU at $46.33, and here's the Jan 2028 chain:

| Strike | Price | IV | Delta | XLU needs to reach | Move needed |
|--------|-------|-----|-------|-------------------|-------------|
| **$55** | $2.33 | 16.7% | 0.36 | $57.33 breakeven | +24% |
| **$57.50** | $1.69 | 16.4% | 0.29 | $59.19 breakeven | +28% |
| **$60** | $1.43 | 17.4% | 0.24 | $61.43 breakeven | +33% |
| **$62.50** | $1.07 | 17.4% | 0.19 | $63.57 breakeven | +37% |
| **$65** | $0.75 | 20.2% | 0.20 | $65.75 breakeven | +42% |
| **$67.50** | $0.73 | 18.5% | 0.14 | $68.23 breakeven | +47% |

**Now the X guy's thesis clicks.** IV is 16-18% on these. That IS cheap. If XLU makes a 40% move to ~$65 by Jan '28:
- The $55C ($2.33) goes to ~$10+ intrinsic = **4-5x**
- The $60C ($1.43) goes to ~$5 intrinsic = **3-4x**
- The $67.50C ($0.73) needs the full move but could **10x** if it gets there

You could buy 10 contracts of the $60C for ~$1,430. If XLU hits $65 that's worth ~$5,000+. If it hits $70 that's $10,000. Defined risk, cheap premium.

The IV mispricing is the real insight — the market is pricing XLU like it's still a boring dividend ETF while the demand fundamentals are transforming underneath it. That's the same pattern Visser describes: the market's risk models are calibrated to the old regime.

Worth a small position. Not the "$100K all-in" the X guy is selling, but a few hundred bucks on the $57.50-$60 strikes is a smart asymmetric bet alongside your existing names. Think about it tomorrow.

## Claude (22:31)

It's 10:28 PM — late, so I'll get this done fast. Here's the Moonshots podcast summary:

---

## Moonshots Podcast Summary

**Guests:** Peter Diamandis, Ben Horowitz (a16z), Alex (Innermost Loop), Dave

### Key Themes

**1. Recursive Self-Improvement Is Here**
AI systems are now improving themselves. Ben Horowitz's investment in SSI (Ilya Sutskever's company) is a bet on this — "if he pulls it off it will change a lot of things." This confirms Visser's thesis that we're in a **new regime**, not a cycle. The pace of disruption accelerates from here.

**2. Capital Wins, Labor Loses**
Wages up +3% vs corporate profits up +43%. Peter's key insight: **rate cuts now buy AI agents/robots instead of hiring humans.** Every rate cut is fuel for automation, not traditional employment. This is structural, not cyclical.

**3. Crypto as AI-Native Money**
- a16z invested in an "AI bank" and **Daylight Energy** (energy trading with crypto + AI)
- Self-replicating AI agents using **Bitcoin Lightning** for machine-to-machine payments
- a16z crypto funds outperforming conventional venture funds
- Thesis: crypto is infrastructure for the agent economy, not speculation

**4. Hardware Demand Surge**
- **Mac Mini / Mac Studio sold out** — people buying them to run OpenClaw and local AI models
- Apple hardware becoming AI hosting infrastructure at consumer price points

**5. Space + AI Convergence**
- SpaceX pivoting from Mars to Moon (mass drivers, AI satellites, eventual Dyson swarm concept)
- **Amazon Kuiper:** 4,500 LEO satellites approved — competing with Starlink
- AI satellites = compute in orbit

**6. Voice as New Interface**
- **11 Labs** achieved human-level speech synthesis
- Voice becomes the primary AI interface (not text, not screens)

**7. Video Generation Maturing**
- ByteDance **Seedance 2.0** — video generation getting commercially viable

---

### Actionable Trade Ideas

| Idea | Rationale | Action |
|------|-----------|--------|
| **AAPL** | Mac Mini/Studio sold out for AI use. Apple is becoming consumer AI hardware platform. Already own — confirms hold. | Hold / watch for pullback entry on LEAPs |
| **Bitcoin / BTC exposure** | AI-native money thesis from a16z. Lightning network for agent payments. Aligns with Visser: BTC works when NASDAQ underperforms. | Watch — enters play when SaaS bottoms |
| **AMZN** | Kuiper 4,500 LEO satellites + AWS. Space-AI convergence. | Already expensive. Note thesis. |

### Watchlist Additions

| Ticker | Why |
|--------|-----|
| **Daylight Energy** | a16z-backed. AI + crypto + energy trading. Private now — watch for IPO/SPAC. |
| **SSI (Ilya's company)** | a16z/Ben invested. Recursive self-improvement play. Private — watch for public investment vehicles. |
| **RKLB (Rocket Lab)** | Space-AI convergence. If SpaceX stays private, RKLB is the public proxy. |

### Thesis Updates

1. **Visser "new regime" — CONFIRMED.** Recursive AI improvement + capital-over-labor dynamic validates that this is structural, not cyclical. Dispersion continues.

2. **Scarcity thesis — REINFORCED.** Hardware demand (Mac Mini sold out), energy demand (Daylight Energy), physical infrastructure (satellites) all confirm: **atoms > bits**. Long scarcity, short abundance.

3. **Software death spiral — CONFIRMED from different angle.** If AI agents work autonomously and pay each other in crypto, the entire SaaS middleware layer gets disintermediated. Ben Horowitz building the agent infrastructure directly.

4. **Crypto thesis — UPGRADE.** Previously treated crypto as speculative. a16z framing it as **infrastructure for autonomous agents** is a stronger thesis. Not "digital gold" — it's machine money. This changes the timeline: crypto becomes investable when agent adoption hits critical mass, not when retail FOMO kicks in.

5. **Rate cuts = automation fuel.** Peter's observation is critical for our macro view: every rate cut that's supposed to stimulate employment actually accelerates replacement of labor with AI/robots. **Bullish for capital owners, bearish for wage earners.** Confirms being on the capital side of every trade.

---

### Bottom Line

The podcast validates our existing framework (Visser's scarcity/abundance, new regime thesis) from a different angle — the builders, not just the analysts. The crypto-as-agent-money thesis is the most novel addition. No immediate trades, but **strengthens conviction on hardware/energy longs and software shorts.**

---

Now get some sleep, Norm. It's 10:30. HYG puts go in Monday morning — fresh eyes.

## Claude (22:52)

Needs a password prompt I can't provide. Easier for you to just grab it from the Mac App Store:

1. **Open App Store on your Mac** → search **Tailscale** → Install (free)
2. **Open Tailscale** → sign in (Google account works)
3. It'll give you a **100.x.x.x** IP — that's your Mac's permanent address from anywhere

Then on your **iPhone**:
1. Install **Tailscale** from the App Store → sign in with the **same account**
2. Install **Termius** from the App Store

Once both devices are on Tailscale, you can SSH into your Mac from anywhere — cell data, coffee shop, anywhere. The 100.x.x.x address never changes.

Also still need: **System Settings → General → Sharing → Remote Login → ON**

This is a 10-minute setup, but it's 10:50 PM. Want to knock it out now or pick it up tomorrow?

## Claude (23:04)

That's the **Dock** at the bottom of the screen. The **menu bar** is the thin strip at the very **top** of the screen — where it shows the Apple logo on the far left, then the app name, and on the right side has the clock, WiFi, battery, etc.

Look up there, top-right corner, near the clock. That's where Tailscale's icon would be.

## Claude (23:04)



That's the **menu bar**. The right side where the icons live (clock, battery, WiFi, Tailscale, etc.) is sometimes called the **menu bar extras** or **system tray** (though system tray is technically a Windows term that people use loosely).
